text:
Good recipe. But I do have a comment on the comments! I am astounded that people change a recipe for a baked item and then complain when it doesn't turn out well. Baking=chemistry. You cannot "decrease the flour and add more peanut butter" without changing the end result! It is not like soup where you can add some of this and take out some of that... soup will still be soup, albeit with a different flavor. Cookies and other baked good rely on fairly precise measurements--you can't just change things without the right sort of re-balancing of ingredients. Ok! End of rant.

text:
These turned out great!  For a Christmas cookie, I replaced 1 cup of chocolate chips with red and green M&Ms.  To get awesome texture, I chilled the dough thorougly, rolled the dough into 1/4 cup size balls, pressed some M&Ms on top, then baked at 350 for about 18 minutes.  Looked like they came from the store bakery!  Oh, and I replaced the corn syrup with honey.

text:
Awesome!  I did as other reviewers did and decreased the flour to about 2 cups and increased the PB to almost 1 cup. I sell my baked goodies for extra cash and these are one of the top sellers! I added toffee bits instead of choco chips.  ***My big secret to successful cookies: ALWAYS substitute 1/2 the ammount of butter called for in any recipe with shortening!!*** This makes them lighter and puff up more while still having the richness from the butter. Also, ALWAYS chill dough first to keep from spreading too much!

text:
After so many glowing reviews and beautiful photos, I don't know what more I can add to this except for another thumbs up,  assuming I have a fair amount of credibility.  These.  Are.  Awesome good.  Thick and plump with appealing raggedy edges and tops. Gooey, chewy,  peanut buttery and sinfully chocolate.  Just looking at them makes you want to grab one and wolf it, and once you do, you're glad you did.  None of the regrets you thought you might have if you did.  These are the cookies GOOD, talented, old-fashioned home cooks used to make (and some of course, still do) and come with all the wonderful memories of some of those cooks, times, tastes and aromas associated with those days.  I can't say enough about these.  You want to know what I changed about the recipe?  Absolutely nothing.  Know what I'll change when I make them again?  You're right - absolutely nothing.  I know some peeps here in Naples who will have very appreciative, chocolaty, smiling faces tonight.  And that makes me happy.

text:
My 3 year old daughter and I made these using the suggested changes of 1 cup PB and lessening the flour to 2 cups.  Instead of chocolate chips we used the Christmas M&Ms and reserved about 1/4 cup of them for her to put on the tops of each cookie.  We also used a smaller cookie scoop (1 TBS?) to make the balls and then kinda flattened them with the spatula as they came out.  They were fun to make together.  I also froze half the dough in a roll to see how that would work out if I ever wanted to make them in large batches.  The only drawback to this is that when you slice the cookies - you inevitably cut some of the M&Ms.  (Also, if you use this method - you can wait till they soften a little on the pan and your kids can still add some M&Ms)

text:
These cookies are wonderful!  They stay nice and gooey, if you want them to.  Or just bake them a little longer for firmer cookies.  I sent a double batch to my husband in Afghanistan, and he said one of his NCOs said they taste like "love all mushed up and baked".  I did change the cookie sizes.  I rolled mine into balls only a little larger than a tablespoon, and only baked them for starting at 9 minutes.  When the bottom edges *just* start to turn golden, take them out for epic gooey goodness.  I baked some a little longer, because my dad loves his crunchy.  This recipe is a keeper.

text:
I customized this recipe based on some of the other comments, and am glad I made these changes:  increased  peanut butter to 1 cup, decreased chocolate to 1 cup, 1-1/2 cups brown sugar (no white), honey instead of corn syrup, and 1 tbsp vanilla.  They are rich tasting, moist, and have a good balance of peanut butter and chocolate.  I plan to give some of these my crush, and I think they'll be a hit!  Note: I used 1/4 c. of dough for each cookie per the directions, but the yield was only 18, not 24.

text:
I've never rated anything under a four on this site, but I have to say the title of this cookie is very misleading. A). It isn't chewy, it's very cake-like and B). It doesn't taste like peanut butter at all. I think that maybe people's definition of a "chewy" cookie must vary, because like one reviewer said, they should rise slightly while cooking and then sink flat while cooling. Slightly underdone in the middle. These maintained their spoonful shape, and even rose a little highter than that. The result was a somewhat dry, cake like cookie that didn't have much peanut butter taste to it. Next time I will search for just a basic peanut butter cookie recipe and add chocolate chips to it.

text:
I was looking for a recipe that duplicated cookies like the ones our local bakery makes, and, boy, did I find it.  Since I was really in the mood for a plain peanut butter cookie, I omitted the chocolate chips and increased the PB to 3/4 cup.  The dough was very soft, so I refrigerated it for about an hour or 2 before baking (baked at 350 degrees for 12-14 minutes).  The texture of these cookies was absolutely perfect!  I think next time I'll try a different brand of PB (used Jif extra crunchy this time).  The crunchiness was great, but I would love a really rich PB taste, and this batch didn't quite have me reaching for a second glass of milk.  Thanks for the recipe.

text:
The dough is nice to work with, as it is light and not tough or sticky like some other cookie recipes.  I use a 1/2 cup less chocolate chips but it all depends on how chocolate chipy you like your cookies.  It's not as peanut buttery as some other peanut butter cookies, but I prefer it this way as the peanut butter taste is not overwhelming.  For a little extra chew you may want to cut 2 minutes off the suggested baking time.  Everyone I gave them to liked it.  I would definitely make this again.  Thanks a lot for sharing. :-)

Really easy and good!  I used 1&1/3cup milk chocolate chips, and pure peanut butter (no other additives).  I was worried they wouldn't be sweet enough using the pure peanut butter but they were great.  The only thing with this recipe (as with all peanut butter cookie recipes) is that you really have to stay close to the oven to make sure the bottoms don't get brown.  I baked them on a pretty low setting (300 degrees) and they were done in about 12 minutes.

The BEST! Slight changes I made; increased PB to 1 cup, used all brown sugar, decreased flour to 2 1/4 cups.  I used a mixture of mini chocolate chips and M&Ms.  Rolled them into balls, flattened ever-so-slightly with a cup dipped in white sugar and topped with a few more M&Ms.  Baked at recommended temp for 11 minutes.  These turned out BEAUTIFUL and TASTED EVEN BETTER.  Yummy!

The title tells no lies, these are perfectly chewy cookies. Great texture and bakes off great (doesn't flatten out in the oven). This is a great pb base for adding mix-ins. Instead of chocolate chips, I put chopped up peanut butter cups in this dough. However, I think it really needs the chocolate chips to set off the peanut butter flavor. Either that or use some dark chocolate peanut butter cups. The combination of more pb/milk chocolate with the pb flavor in this cookie just struck me as a little bland.

text:
This recipe works as a base for a good chewy peanutbutter cookie...
Changes:
-Double peanut butter if you reall like to have the taste, I also use chunky to give the cookie more texture
-Take out 1/2 cup flour
-1/2 the amount of chocolate chips
-An I personally like to use honey instead of corn syrup.
We also had to bake longer but our oven tends to be that way for everything.  
After the changes I would give the recipe a 4 stars (I think I would use a little less surgar and add even more peanutbutter next time)

I really enjoyed this recipe.  I also used Peanut M&M's as one reviewer suggested and instead of using what is commonly called peanut butter these days, I used the all natural peanut butter.  The combination added a wonderful salty/chocolatly flavor, satisfying the salty/sweet craving.  I did find that 1/4 cupfull was a bit big.  The middles stayed a big too gooey for my taste, but friends said they liked them that way.  I'll be making these again, perhaps a bit smaller.  All and all, I think this is my new favorite peanut butter cookie recipe.

text:
I increased the peanut butter by another 1/2 cup. They turned out moist and perfect but I would have like a little more of a peanut butter flavor. I read some of the reviews saying they cooked quickly on the outside and were not completely done on the inside. This will be true if you don't flatten your cookie a bit. There may be chocolate but this is after all still a peanut butter cookie recipe and we don't just press our peanut butter cookies with forks so they look pretty. Any peanut butter cookie recipe would yield the same result if you simply left it in a pile. I rolled them into balls then flattened the cookie in the palm of my hand (I did not use the quarter cup). I will make these again and reduce the flour by 1/2 cup and keep the peanut butter at 1 cup to see if it can get a flavor boost. I am impressed with how soft these stayed.

text:
Everyone loves these cookies!! I have read reviews and tweaked it as I've kept making it but, to me, that's just what happens when a lot of people bake the same thing! I DOUBLE the peanut butter because, even doubled, it is not overwhelming peanut butter. I reduce the flour by 1/4 cup. I switch the brown sugar and white sugar measurements...I have found that doing this makes them look more like a cookie and less like a ball! I chill the dough in the freezer (because I am impatient!) for 10 min. before and then in the 'fridge while another sheet bakes. I use a cookie scoop--much faster! I bake them for 10 min. at 375....and they turn out perfectly! So CHEWY and delicious! I have been told I should sell them in a bakery! Mmmm!

text:
This recipe was good, but I made some slight changes. I didn't have corn syrup, so I used 1 tbsp of light maple syrup, and one tbsp of honey. I changed the cooking time as well to 7 minutes because leaving them in for longer makes them a little too crunchy for my liking. When you put the dough on the pan, press it down just a little bit and keep them in for about 7 minutes. They turned out delicious with the modifications I used. Hope this helps you too!

While I thought these were just "ok", everyone at work thought they were absolutely delicious. I did change 4 things... text:
This was a wonderfully easy cookie to make.  I followed the original recipe exactly - but did take Dianne's advice and added a cup of red and green M&M's to make them more festive for the holidays.  No need to chill the dough or roll them - just dropped them by large spoon fulls and add more M&M's to the top.    The recipe makes exactly 24 nice adult palm sized cookies.  They cooked up well in my oven at exactly 13 minutes and were soft and chewy to eat.  Big hit with the kids.  They taste like choc chips cookies with a nice sized hint of peanut butter.    These cookies look and taste great.  Will definately make again.  Double batch next time to share with others.  Great Christmas tin cookie for sure.

You don't need to 'know how' to write a review in order to tell people your thoughts on how a recipe tasted to you, or how it turned out for you.  I will agree, these cookies have a very subtle peanut butter taste, but I and many others (a truckload of children included!) have never found them bitter; always soft, chewy and delicious!  In my opinion, this recipe is perfect the way it is unless you do want a stronger peanut butter flavor, and in this case you can just substitute some of the butter for more peanut butter.  This recipe is a very standard drop cookie format, and with some attention to detail and practice, the cookies should always turn out amazing!

text:
This one is a keeper. I made it the first time to give away and was anxious about changing anything. So I made it precisely as given.  The size portions (1/4 c.) surprised me as I normally use a small scoop tool (approx 1 heaping T.) for cookies.  I 'adjusted' by dropping two scoops per cookie. I underbaked the first pan as some reviewers cut down the time. Those were gooey and melty. At 12 minutes baking and a good 3 minutes cooling they were perfect; soft but complete. The only 'complaint' I heard was, "There's peanut butter in there? I don't taste any peanut butter." Overall, though, everybody wants 'em again.

This is a decent recipe however the temperature of the baking will ruin your cookies.

Everyone knows cookies are baked at 350 degrees not 375.   To prove it I baked at 375 for 12 to 15 min at 12 min bottom was burnt slightly 15 min bottoms all burnt.

This is an easy fix however for those non bakers following the directions perfectly will ensure you get burnt bottoms.

text:
Soo good! I am glad i didnt listen to the negative reviews. DONT change a thing unless its just the chips. I did half reese chips and half semisweet. I use a 4 tbsp scoop to make big cookies. I bake my cookies at 325 on a light colored pan with parchment paper. These took 15 min. Right when i took them out i pressed the tops with a spatula (they rise a lot like a muffin almost). I let them sit on the pan for about 5 min before transfering to rack. They are best the next day in my opinion. I am more of a "chocolate chip cookie right out of the oven" person. These are good warm, but awesome maybe say 12 hours later. So 5 stars....dont change the flour, pb, honey, etc etc DONT do all that. And they ARE soft and chewy.

I was looking for a peanut butter cookie recipe to use up some peanut butter.  Also wanted to add chocolate chips.  Found this recipe and it was exactly what I was looking for.  Followed exactly except doubled it.  The cookies were great but the chocolate chips overpowered the peanut butter - not a problem, just wanted to use up some peanut butter. text:
Ok I just made these tonight. I used chocolate chips instead of chocolate chunks. I didn't measure the amount of chips I just eyeballed it. I also substituted thick sugar water for the corn syrup because I didn't have any. Other than that the only thing I changed was the cookie size and bake time. I used my Tablespoon measuring spoon and made rounded scoops. It made almost 3 dozen. It might have made the full three dozen but I have a cookie dough addiction. I also only baked them for 11 minutes. the 1st batch I did for 9 but I had to put them back in. even after they were still not quite right they wanted to fall apart. the other two I put in for 11 minutes and they were perfect.They were not dry at all and I did not reduce the flour a bit. I do recommenced chilling the dough after mixing for less messy scooping though. I also kept in the fridge while baking previous batches. The kids love them... thanks for posting. Oh yes someone mentioned the type of peanut butter might make a difference in how they turn out... I don't know if it does or not but I use Skippy natural creamy.

These were a HUGE hit with my three kids (and one kid visitor), especially the 7-year-old who has told me at least three times that these are the best cookies he's ever had in his entire life. I kept the recipe exactly as stated except cut back the sugar to 1 cup (of demerara sugar; I don't keep white or brown sugar on hand) and cut the chocolate chips to 1 cup. I weighed the balls of dough, using about 50 grams per cookie and they baked perfectly in 11 minutes. They taste great and look awesome, just the way a "perfect cookie" should look. I will be making these again and again!

These are sooo delicious! I have made them twice now and they disappear so fast. Based on other reviews I made the following changes: I used 1 cup of peanut butter, honey instead of corn syrup, 1 1/2 cups of chocolate chips (the first time I used the full 2 cups, but it was just too much, there were extra choc. chips at the bottom of the bowl that wouldn't mix w/ the dough). I baked at 350 for about 14 mins. They are great the next day - they stay perfectly soft if you put them in an air tight container. I had several people beg me for the recipe :p

text:
First off I didn't have any corn syrup so I thought why not use light molasses but dared to only put in one teaspoon. Dropped small amounts of dough on cookie sheet and baked for nine minutes and let cool for one minute before removing. The texture was so light and fluffy, definitely not for the crisp cookie folks. My cookies looked like the picture - I flattened the dough slightly before baking. And, I had left my butter out to soften and it was near a heat vent, still in its bar form but so melty when I prepped the cookies. Can't understand why some had trouble with their dough, I'm usually the one with flat cookies. Nice p.b. flavor, not overpowering, I might add chopped peanuts or brickle bits next time for added texture. Yum! Update: not as happy with this cookie the following day, seemed dry and tasteless as opposed to how good it was fresh from the oven. Agree with others now, that more peanut butter may be the answer.

text:
Pretty rockin recipe, let's start with my changes.  I just used half a container of PB (I hate measuring things), definitely use honey instead of corn syrup (yum!), I like to cut the APF with some whole wheat flour to put some (ok, very little) nutrition into the recipe and it helps let the cookies spread out a bit more when being cooked.  I used a cookie ice cream scoop thing to make them all equal sized balls.  I used "White Chocolate Wonderful" Peanut Butter (it's ridonkulously delish) and ommitted the chocolate in lieu of a single white chocolate chip on the top of each ball.  10min, center of over, @ 375, they were perfect.  True story, before I even got out of the kitchen, I already had 3 engagement requests.  Ladies love em.

I decided to not use the recipe that i usually use, you know trying something new. My initial misgivings regarding the sugar to flour ratio and the peanut butter to flour ratio were right on. I had thought, oh corn syrup, maybe that'll make up for the differences. Results: Dry, Not chewy in the least, Does not flatten or spread while baking. The pre-baked texture is like a refrigerator roll cookie. The ratio of flour to both sugar and peanut butter is too high. Also with the peanut butter ratio being so low, it is only marginally a peanut butter cookie, each cookie features a cruel tease of peanut butter. I'm not trying to be cruel in kind. It's just that the results simply do  match the description. A possible fix would be to increase PB by one cup and sugar by a cup possibly then increasing baking soda by a half tablespoon but i'd only try that after tweaking the PB and sugar content.

These are delicious. One mistake people may make is not weighing the flour. Packing it in the measuring cup will add too much flour and create a dry cookie. I often crave peanut butter things and Jif worked well with this recipe. I decreased the chocolate chips by 1/2 cup, used Earth Balance in place of the butter, flax eggs in place of chicken eggs, and played with the cooking time. Eleven minutes seemed to be ideal. I lightly pressed the cookies down before baking which made them more attractive in my opinion.

text:
I just made these cookies for our quilt guild meeting.  OMG!  They are so delicious!  The only changes I made to the original recipe is I pressed them down with a fork and  baked them for 15 minutes as they are very thick. I used creamy peanut butter and chopped up about one cup of unsalted peanuts. The dough gets very thick as you add the last of the flour and the chocolate chips and chopped peanuts. You may have to change out to your bread hook on your mixer at the very end. I doubled the batch so there will be enough for every one at quilt guild meeting.  The picture is from the first two cookie sheets I baked.  It made approx. 4 dozen when doubled. They are like the monster cookies you buy at the bakery or supermarket deli!

text:
Took the advice of other reviewers and used a little over 1 cup of peanut butter, reduced the flour to 2 cups, and used 1 1/2 cups semi-sweet chocolate chips. I refrigerated the dough overnight to make it easier to work with. I made the cookies into thick disks before baking and it worked out that they didn't stay too mounded, nor did they spread too much. I used parchment paper (lifesaver!). My temp and time were different depending on the pan (dark vs light) so it's best if you know the personality of your oven and bakeware to get the right doneness. If I make these again, I might leave out the flour altogether, and will use even less chocolate chips. I do like the large size cookies. My husband said, "What's wrong with big cookies?" He's right, nothing!

text:
For me, these cookies were too sweet. For my husband, they were the best thing ever. If I made them again for myself, I would use more peanut butter, use a little less sugar, leave out the corn syrup entirely, and add a 1/4 tsp more salt. Also, these cookies DO NOT spread. They will stay the exact shape they are put onto the cookie sheet. The first batch I made (using a cookie scoop), stayed in a mound shape, and weren't done in the middle even though the bottom of the cookies were browned. The second batch, I flattened the cookies and they were perfectly cooked after 13 minutes in the oven.

text:
These are the peanut butter cookies I remember as a child. Yummy!  
This recipe easily makes three dozen but, of course it depends on how big you make your cookies. I made two dozen about the size of a ping pong ball and the last dozen (I got tired) more like a golf ball size. Because the cookies don't spread (just like any peanut butter cookie sans the fork marks) I slightly mashed down the balls before baking them. I baked one batch for 11minutes, the second for 9 minutes and the third for 10 minutes. 10 was just right as they came out brown on the bottom, more done in the middle bu still chewy. This week ll all depend on your oven-mine cooks a little hotter. Also, I didn't chop my chocolate chips (why all that work?) but only added 11/2 cup of chips. Actually I could have cut it down the o 1 1/4 and there would of have been plenty. All and all this was a great, simple, and tasty recipe.

https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/5674136.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
Great, basic cookie dough.  There is less peanut butter in these cookies than what I would call true peanut butter cookies, so the texture of the center of cookie is more chewy than traditional peanut butter cookies.  The baked cookie also tastes a bit less peanut-buttery.  This cookie dough lends itself to many possibilities for substitution of the chocolate chips with any sort of nut and/or dried fruit.  A good ratio might be half nuts and half chips/dried fruit to achieve the correct balance of sweetness. You could also go a bit heavier on the chip/nut/dried fruit combination if you prefer (like I do).  I made mine with 1/4 cup of dough for each cookie and I pressed the center of each with the 1/4 cup measuring cup (I did not sugar the cup before pressing).  They would have been prettier if I had also scored them with a fork or potato masher.  I baked for 12-14 min at the recommended temperature.  I froze them as soon as they were cooled in individual zip lock sandwich bags so they are easy to grab for on-the-go lunchbags.  I will be making these again, probably with cranberries, butterscotch chips and walnuts, a combination my family loves.

text:
Delicious and easy.   I used a dough scoop (looks like a small ice cream scoop) to drop the cookie dough onto silpat lined baking sheet.  The first dozen I didn't press down,  I just baked them in that form, kinda rounded for about 12 minutes and they were fluffy and soft.  Still chewy and delicious .  For the next dozen, I still used the scoop, but this time I made the classic criss cross with a fork as you would do with regular peanut butter cookies and baked the full 14 minutes.   These were a bit crispy around the edges, but still chewy in the middle in their flattend state, more crunch.  Both ways, this cookie was awesome.   Also, I used butter flavor cisco in place of the butter, and used half dark chocolate morsels and half regular chocolate chips.  I will definitely add this to my cookie rapport and it is sure to quickly became a favorite!

text:
Oh my!  We're cookie monsters at our house, and this was a superb recipe! I profited from some of the other reviewers who tweaked the recipe a bit.  I used close to 3/4 cup chunky natural peanut butter.  I did not pack the brown sugar, just spoon/pour it in the cup.  Experience has proven that one can decrease the sugar in most cookie recipes by 1/4 cup with no noticeable loss in flavor.  I used 2 T. honey instead of corn syrup, and 1-1/2 cups of chocolate chips.  I mixed mini chips and regular sized ones.  350 degrees for 12 minutes was just perfect in my oven.  I have a multitude of cookie recipes, and this is one of the best, texture and taste. You're right, they are addictive.  Thanks Kathy.  I will definitely pass this one on!

text:
These are great cookies! I followed the recipe exactly and they turned out wonderful. I didn't use a 1/4 cup measure for dipping up the cookies; used a tablespoon and my cookies were slightly smaller than the recipe. I got 4 1/2 dozen cookies. They smelled like peanut butter cookies while baking and tasted like peanut butter cookies when eaten. I use quality peanut butter, though--not store brand. My first pan baked a little long so were a little more crispy than chewy, but the rest were nice and chewy. Keep an eye on the clock after the pan is out of the oven and be sure to take up the cookies or they will become welded to the baking sheet. Thanks for a delicious recipe!

text:
This recipe is OK.  I have made it several times as I like more chew in my cookies.  The first time I made it it came out pretty good.  The last few times it was  too thick and cake like.  The only difference was I used a gas oven the first time.  Like others have stated there is no real peanut butter flavor, only a hint of it.  I would reduce flour by 1/2 cup or until texture is right.  Also leaving the dough in the fridge over night helps to meld the butter/sugar with the flour better and the cookies don't come out quite so fluffy. On the up side I can leave these cookies out for a couple of days and they don't get rock hard.

I used mini chocolate chips and dropped them by a regular-sized cookie scoop and baked for 10 minutes - they look like they came from a bakery.  I'll definitely make these again!

text:
These are definitely soft and chewy, but very plain tasting (I really can't taste the peanut butter at all). 

I have allergies so I had to make a couple of substitutions, and those could have made all the difference to the flavour. I replaced the butter with canola oil and used natural unsweetened peanut butter (the kind you have to keep in the fridge). I think part of the "plain" taste is from not having enough peanut butter in the recipe and also because with unsweetened peanut butter, more sugar is required (which I did not add - 1.5 cups seemed like plenty!). Next time I would try adding more peanut butter and more sugar and a little more salt.

text:
If you like peanut butter and chocolate, you need to try this! It's an easy recipe if you want to try something a little different than regular chocolate chip cookies. I liked this recipe, the cookies came out very chewy but I took them out before they were fully cooked because I didn't want to have them too dry. I didn't have enough chocolate chips, so instead of all chocolate chips about a quarter of the chocolates were the Wilton's candy melts in light cocoa. I think this was a great idea because the chocolate melted inside the cookie and even after cooling they were still gooey when you bit into it! You should try this if you like a gooey consistency in your cookies! Yummy!

Sad thing was, I think 375 degrees was a tad too hot for the fat content and the bottoms of the cookies got really dark - almost burnt! This recipe is a keeper!!!

Most good-looking cookies I've ever made. And perhaps the most delicious, too.

I used unsalted almond butter instead of peanut butter, which is very very subtle, but adds to the "heartiness" of the cookies.

I baked for 6 minutes, rotated, 6 minutes. Perfect.

I will definitely makes these again --

I am rating this 4 stars, not because it's a bad cookie, but because this recipe, on its own is nothing special. I made the recipe verbatim, and they were only so-so. After tweaking it a bit, it turned out amazing!

Thanks!

I can't fault the recipe, because I followed it exactly (with the exception of using chips instead of chopped chocolate but I wouldn't think that should affect the taste) and the cookies turned out fine. It's just that when I hear the word "chewy" I'm thinking more of your typical moist, dense, traditional chocolate chip cooke texture, and the most accurate word for these, I think, is "fluffy". I made these cookies based on the other rave reviews and made them gluten free! They worked wonderfully! I cut down the butter and increased the peanut butter, also used natural peanut butter. I cut the flour down as well as I always find gluten free to be heavier as it is, and so are most peanut butter cookies! I also substituted agave nectar in place of corn syrup and they still turned out awesome!!! Very happy with them, gluten free can be tricky, but these cookies passed the test!

text:
These were very good, you cant taste the peanut butter at all ! But they were chewy. I didt have light corn sypup so I made my own. Here is the recipe:2 cups white sugar 3/4 cup water 1/4 tsp cream of tartar dash of salt. combine all ingredients in a heavy large pan. Sir and bring to a boil.Reduce heat to a simmer and put cover on it for 3 mins to get sugar cystals off the sides of the pan. Uncover and cook until it reaches soft ball stage. stir often.Cool syrup and store in a covered container at room temperture. It will keep for about 2 months. Makes almost  2 cups.

text:
These are getting a 5 because although I had to tweak it a little my boyfriend loved them.  He said they are the best cookies I've made to date and I bake ALOT.  After reading alot of the reviews and having a bunch of people say the same thing about them not having enough p-nut butter I increased that.  I used a cup of creamy p-nut butter and a 1/4 cup of crunchy.  I also used 1 cup of p-nut butter chips and 1 cup of chocolate chips.  I also only put mine in for 9 mins.  They were perfect!  Just enough p-nut butter taste.  Also, just the right texture or chewiness.  Thanx for the great recipe and thanx to all for the suggestions!  A definite keeper!!

text:
I would give this 3 1/2 stars if I could.  These cookies had a nice flavor, but I was not overly impressed with them, and I have definitely tasted better.  The second time around I added 1 cup of quick oats in place of 1 cup of flour and this made the texture better.  I only cooked mine for 10 minutes - any longer than that and they ended up very crispy, not at all soft.  They do spread - they are not puffy cookies after they have cooled.  I may make this again, but I think I will probably keep looking for a softer peanut butter cookie.

text:
wow, wow, wow!  These were so fabulous.  Just like Starbucks cookies.  I made some changes based on reviews and on what I was trying to simulate (the peanut butter cup cookies from the Barnes and Noble Starbucks).  I used 1/4 C butter and 1/4 C coconut oil instead of 1/2 C butter.  I cut the sugar down to 1 1/4 C total (next time I'll go down to 1 C).  I used honey instead of corn syrup.  I used about 3/4 C of peanut butter, and cut the flour down to 2C (I also used all whole wheat flour instead of white).  I used 1 C of semi-sweet choc chips and about 3/4 C of Reece's pueanut butter cup morsels (like tiny peanut butter cups).  These made big delicious cookies, I will deffinently make this again and might even freeze the cookies so I'm not tempted to buy Starbucks cookies next time we go there.

text:
Fantastic cookies!  I doubled the recipe and dropped the batter by the tablespoon, winding up with around 65 cookies or so.  Changes I made: I omitted the chocolate chunks, reduced the flour by 1/2 cup, added 1/2 cup more peanut butter, and used skim milk in place of the water.  They still don't have a very strong peanut butter taste, but they are delicious.  They spread into thin, 3" circles that are soft and chewy with lightly crispy edges.  Highly recommended!
